Hence, the truly wise are luminous yet not dazzling, hence not broadly learned. The broadly learned are superficial in sight, hence lack true knowledge.

The Sage does not hoard. The more one gives to others, the more one possesses; the more one shares, the more one has. Master Lü said: *The Zhuangzi* speaks of the Dao’s movement without accumulation, thus all under heaven revere it. The Sage’s "not hoarding" means spreading virtue for others—those who receive it see their virtue grow ever brighter, like a mirror’s clarity, never diminished. To distribute wealth to the poor: the poor accept the gift, yet the giver’s wealth grows ever fuller, like a wellspring’s clear, unending flow, from which all things draw without depletion. Master Liezi said that giving wealth is the mark of an accomplished person, while sharing virtue is the mark of the Sage—both embody "not hoarding."

Because there is accumulation, there is lack; because there is no hoarding, there is abundance. Hence, *"The Sage does not hoard; the more one gives to others, the more one possesses; the more one shares, the more one has."*

Master He said: Why does the Sage not hoard? *The Zhuangzi* says the Dao moves without accumulation, thus all things flourish. The Sage acts without hoarding, thus all under heaven revere them. Hence, *"Because there is accumulation, there is lack; because there is no hoarding, there is abundance."* The Sage’s giving to others only increases their own abundance, sharing with others only multiplies their own wealth—whether through virtue or wealth, demonstrating sincerity, doing good for others, accumulating yet dispersing, broadly learned yet transforming—all embody the intent of making the world public.

Master Lin said: The Sage’s Dao is but emptiness and unity—what is there to hoard? They never fail to benefit others, yet their own abundance grows ever greater. They never fail to share with others, yet their own wealth multiplies evermore. It is like the Dao of Heaven: empty yet unyielding, moving yet ever producing. To benefit others and be benefited in return, to speak the Dao and transform things—this is the Dao of Heaven.

*"The Dao of Heaven benefits all without harming.
The Sage’s Dao acts without strife."*

Master Lü said: The Dao of Heaven is the Yang—it loves life and abhors killing, hence is beneficial without harm. Spring and summer nurture growth; autumn and winter bring maturation. In its utter impartiality, it fulfills what is good in people yet does not complete what is evil. It gives benefit to all without inflicting harm. Hence, *"The Dao of Heaven benefits all without harming."*

Heaven speaks not yet responds perfectly, always answering with substance, not with empty words. The Sage embodies this as harmony, establishes it as practice, and applies it—thus aligned with Heaven, in accord with the Sage. This is the *"six penetrations and four openings,"* the root of all things, yet without strife.

Master He said: The Dao of Heaven benefits all without harm; the Sage’s Dao accomplishes all without strife.

The *Yì* says: **"Qián** [the Creative, Heaven] begins with the power to bring beauty and benefit to the world—yet does not speak of what it benefits. How vast it is! The primal essence of Qián is firm and strong, balanced and upright, a pure and refined concentration of *qi*. Clouds move, rain falls—all things are at peace.**

The Sage who embodies Qián [the Creative] fulfills the Dao completely and brings beauty to all. With boundless generosity, he aids and rescues the people, accomplishing much yet never striving—all from the wondrous application of the Qián essence.

In the final chapter of *Lǎozǐ* [Laozi], the first words are removed, then the Sage and the people are discussed, finally aligning with the Dao of Heaven and the Sage. Their functions are thus fully expressed—is this not already complete?

To know *Yì* [the *Yijing*] is to know *Lǎozǐ* [Laozi].

○ **Lín Shì** said: The Dao of Heaven, though it brings beauty and benefit without speaking of what it benefits, is seen only as beneficial and without harm. If one speaks of its benefiting, then harm also becomes apparent. The Sage’s Dao is effortless yet accomplishes all, yet he never relies on his own power—thus he does not contend with things, yet the world cannot contend with him.

The essence of this text is largely centered on *non-contention*—hence it concludes with these words.

○ **Lǐ Shì** said: The greatest *virtue/power* of Heaven and Earth is *generation*—hence it is said, *"benefit without harm."* The Sage upholds his station with *rén* [benevolence/heart-mind]—hence it is said, *"accomplish without contention."*

If one practices the principle of *non-contention* in daily life, over time and with purity, one will naturally attain the realm of *Hùn Yuán* [the Primordial Chaos], the *true constant Dao*, and reach its utmost perfection. This is the foundation of the *Emperor’s* [the Sage’s] first manifestation, the source of profound clarity—it is achieved.

The *True Scripture of the Dao and Virtue* [the *Daodejing*] concludes its compilation of meaning in the tenth volume.
